#METABOLOMICS WORKBENCH BPnorman_20220124_072035 DATATRACK_ID:3049 STUDY_ID:ST002082 ANALYSIS_ID:AN003396 PROJECT_ID:PR001322
VERSION             	1
CREATED_ON             	February 3, 2022, 2:42 am
#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Predicting dying: a study of the metabolic changes and the dying process in
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	patients with lung cancer
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	Background: Accurately recognising that a person may be dying is central for
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	improving their experience of care. Yet recognising dying is difficult and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	predicting dying frequently inaccurate. Methods: Serial urine samples from
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	patients (n=112) with lung cancer were analysed using high resolution untargeted
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	mass spectrometry. ANOVA and volcano plot analysis demonstrated metabolites that
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	changed in the last weeks of life. Further analysis identified potential
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	biological pathways affected. Cox lasso logistic regression was engaged to
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	develop a multivariable model predicting the probability of survival within the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	last 30 days of life. Results: In total 124 metabolites changed. ANOVA analysis
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	identified 93 metabolites and volcano plot analysis 85 metabolites. 53
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	metabolites changed using both approaches. Pathways altered in the last weeks
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	included those associated with decreased oral intake, muscle loss, decreased RNA
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	and protein synthesis, mitochondrial dysfunction, disrupted β-oxidation and one
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	carbon metabolism. Epinephrine and cortisol increased in the last 2 weeks and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	week respectively. A model predicting time to death using 7 metabolites had
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	excellent accuracy (AUC= 0.86 at day 30, 0.88 at day 20 and 0.85 at day 10) and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	enabled classification of patients at low, medium and high risk of dying on a
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	Kaplan-Meier survival curve. Conclusions: Metabolomic analysis identified
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	metabolites and their associated pathways that change in the last weeks and days
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	of life in patients with lung cancer. Prognostic tests based on the metabolites
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	identified have the potential to change clinical practice and improve the care
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	of dying patients.
PR:INSTITUTE                     	University of Liverpool Institute of Life Course Medical Sciences
PR:LAST_NAME                     	Norman
PR:FIRST_NAME                    	Brendan
PR:ADDRESS                       	William Henry Duncan Building, 6 West Derby Street, Liverpool, Merseyside, L7
PR:ADDRESS                       	8TX, United Kingdom
PR:EMAIL                         	bnorman@liv.ac.uk
PR:PHONE                         	(+44)151 794 9064

PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	and a North West Cancer Research award (SI2018.11)
PR:CONTRIBUTORS                  	Séamus Coyle, Elinor Chapman, David Hughes, James Baker, Andrew S Davison,

#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Predicting dying: a study of the metabolic changes and the dying process in
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	patients with lung cancer
ST:STUDY_TYPE                    	Observational study
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Background: Accurately recognising that a person may be dying is central for
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	improving their experience of care. Yet recognising dying is difficult and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	predicting dying frequently inaccurate. Methods: Serial urine samples from
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	patients (n=112) with lung cancer were analysed using high resolution untargeted
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	mass spectrometry. ANOVA and volcano plot analysis demonstrated metabolites that
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	changed in the last weeks of life. Further analysis identified potential
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	biological pathways affected. Cox lasso logistic regression was engaged to
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	develop a multivariable model predicting the probability of survival within the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	last 30 days of life. Results: In total 124 metabolites changed. ANOVA analysis
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	identified 93 metabolites and volcano plot analysis 85 metabolites. 53
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	metabolites changed using both approaches. Pathways altered in the last weeks
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	included those associated with decreased oral intake, muscle loss, decreased RNA
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	and protein synthesis, mitochondrial dysfunction, disrupted β-oxidation and one
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	carbon metabolism. Epinephrine and cortisol increased in the last 2 weeks and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	week respectively. A model predicting time to death using 7 metabolites had
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	excellent accuracy (AUC= 0.86 at day 30, 0.88 at day 20 and 0.85 at day 10) and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	enabled classification of patients at low, medium and high risk of dying on a
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Kaplan-Meier survival curve. Conclusions: Metabolomic analysis identified
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	metabolites and their associated pathways that change in the last weeks and days
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	of life in patients with lung cancer. Prognostic tests based on the metabolites
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	identified have the potential to change clinical practice and improve the care
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	of dying patients.

#COLLECTION
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	The study was conducted at six sites (hospitals and hospices) in the North West
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	of England (UK) from June 2016 to September 2018. Patients with lung cancer were
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	recruited prospectively and multiple urine samples were collected up to three
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	times a week while an inpatient. Ethical approval was provided by North Wales
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	(West) Research Ethics Committee (REC reference 15/WA/0464). Research team
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	members collected 20 mL of urine from participants in a universal container.
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	For those participants with a urinary catheter, the urine was collected using a
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	needle and syringe from the catheter port. The samples were stored on site in a
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	locked freezer at −20°C. An anonymised record of the medication administered
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	was collected. Collection protocol described previously by Coyle et al. (BMJ
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	Open. 2016; 6(11) e011763. doi: 10.1136/bmjopen-2016-011763).
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	Urine
CO:VOLUMEORAMOUNT_COLLECTED      	20 mL
CO:STORAGE_CONDITIONS            	-20℃
#TREATMENT
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	Clinical observational study. Serial urine samples collected from patients with
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	lung cancer in a palliative care setting at varying time points up until death;
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	&gt;12 weeks - 1 week before death (see 'study design' information). Although
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	multiple samples were collected from patients, only the final sample was
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	included in the analysis.
#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Individual patient samples were thawed at room temperature, vortexed and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	separated into four replicate aliquots in individual 96-well plates (Waters, UK)
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	which were stored at -80 °C until analysis by one of four different methods;
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	two different chromatography conditions in negative and positive ionisation
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	polarity. Pooled quality control samples were created following the protocol
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	described by Norman et al. (Clin Chem. 2019;65(4):530-39. doi:
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	10.1373/clinchem.2018.295345). For each sample group (time before death), a
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	separate representative pool was created by pooling an equal volume of each
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	individual urine sample for quality control purposes. An overall pool was also
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	created by pooling equal proportions of the above group pools. Analysis of
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	individual and pooled samples was performed following dilution of 1:3
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	urine:deionised water (DIRECT-Q 3UV Millipore water purification system) as
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	previously described by Norman et al. (2019).
#CHROMATOGRAPHY
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY        	LC method 1: employed an Atlantis dC18 column (3x100 mm, 3 µm, Waters, UK)
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY        	maintained at 60 °C with flow rate at 0.4 mL/min. Mobile phases were (A) water
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY        	and (B) methanol both containing 5 mmol/L ammonium formate and 0.1 % formic
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY        	acid. The elution gradient started at 5 % B at 0 to 1 min increasing linearly to
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY        	100 % by 12 min, held at 100 % B until 14 min, returning to 95 % A for 5 min.
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_TYPE           	Reversed phase
CH:INSTRUMENT_NAME               	Agilent 6550
CH:COLUMN_NAME                   	Waters Atlantis dC18 (3x100 mm, 3 µm)
#ANALYSIS
AN:ANALYSIS_TYPE                 	MS
#MS
MS:INSTRUMENT_NAME               	Agilent 6550 QTOF
MS:INSTRUMENT_TYPE               	QTOF
MS:MS_TYPE                       	ESI
MS:ION_MODE                      	NEGATIVE
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Mass spectrometry conditions: The mass spectrometer was tuned and calibrated
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	according to protocols recommended by the manufacturer. Acquisition was
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	performed in 2 GHz mode and mass range 50-1700. The capillary voltage was 4000 V
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	and fragmentor voltage 380 V. The desolvation gas temperature was 200 °C with
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	flow rate at 15 L/min. The sheath gas temperature was 300 °C with flow rate at
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	12 L/min. The nebulizer pressure was 40 psig and nozzle voltage 1000 V (± for
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	positive and negative ionisation modes). The acquisition rate was 3
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	spectra/second. The reference mass solution was continually infused at a flow
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	rate of 0.5 mL/min by a separate isocratic pump for constant mass correction.
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Repeat injections of each pooled sample were interspersed throughout the
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	analytical sequence, as per the quality control procedure described by Norman et
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	al. (Clin Chem. 2019;65(4):530-539. doi: 10.1373/clinchem.2018.295345). The
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	individual sample analysis order was randomised computationally. Data
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Pre-processing and Quality Control: All data were acquired using the MassHunter
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	suite (Agilent build 6.0) with quality checks being performed by Qualitative
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Analysis (build 07.00). Mass accuracy was checked using extracted ion
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	chromatograms of reference masses: the resulting accuracy was ±5 ppm during the
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	run. Additionally, chromatographic reproducibility was checked by overlaying
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	binary pump pressure curves across each analytical sequence. Data was filtered
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	based upon the pooled QC samples, with compounds being retained if observed in
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	100 % of replicate injections for at least 1 pool and with peak area coefficient
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	of variation (CV) &lt;25 % across all replicate injections for each pool. A
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	comprehensive semi-targeted approach was employed to assign the identity of
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	urinary metabolites using an in-house compound library that included a broad
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	range of metabolites involved in intermediary metabolism. Targeted feature
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	extraction was performed on each dataset based on matching of metabolite
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	chemical features against an accurate mass and retention time (AMRT) database
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	previously generated from analysis of the IROA Technology MS metabolite library
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	of tandards by each LC method described above, combined with the same QTOF
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	analytical parameters used in this study (databases publicly available:
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	https://doi.org/10.6084/m9.figshare.c.4378235.v2). In addition to accurate mass
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	and retention time, MS/MS (data-dependent, employed for 'hit' metabolites) was
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	also used in the confirmation of metabolite identity (i.e. level 1
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	identification) as per Sumner et al. Feature extraction was performed in
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	MassHunter Profinder (build 10.0); accurate mass window of 10 ppm and retention
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	time window of 0.3 min against the respective AMRT database. Data were exported
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	in the format of a csv file for statistical analysis. Unidentified compounds are
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	'known unknowns' of interest from previous experiments; detection by matched
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	AMRT and named in the format 'RT_neutral-mass'. 'BDRM'; unidentified
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	bone-derived metabolite.
